**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) with an aromatic ring (e.g., benzoic acid derivatives) tend to result in high yield. This is likely due to the electron-withdrawing nature of the aromatic ring, which can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-aminobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure, particularly those with an additional functional group such as an indole or phenyl group, tend to result in high yield. This could be due to the ability of these groups to coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalyst's activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield. The thiol group can strongly coordinate with metal centers, potentially enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. Examples: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield. The basicity of the pyridine nitrogen might interfere with the catalyst's active site, reducing its effectiveness. Examples: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of the CF3 group might destabilize the catalyst or interfere with the reaction mechanism. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[Br]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid with aromatic and electron-withdrawing group
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]', '[n]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic or heteroaromatic
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol group
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 8: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 9: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid group
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]']  # Rule 10: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 2, the SMARTS pattern '[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]', '[n]' may not accurately capture the presence of an amino acid with additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups. Consider using a pattern that captures the amino acid backbone with aromatic side chains, such as '[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][c,n]'.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern '[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' should be revised to ensure it captures thiol groups effectively. Consider using a pattern like '[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' to ensure the thiol group is directly connected to the carboxylic acid group.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 4, the SMARTS pattern '[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]' may not effectively capture sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyl groups. Consider using a pattern that captures the cyclic nature and multiple hydroxyl groups, such as '[C@H]1([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]1[OX2H]'.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 5, the SMARTS pattern '[n]1ccccc1' is correct for pyridine rings, but ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly parsed to identify pyridine structures.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS pattern '[CX4](F)(F)F' is correct for trifluoromethyl groups, but ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly parsed to identify these groups.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3H]=O' should be revised to ensure it captures aldehyde groups on aromatic rings effectively. Consider using a pattern like '[c][CX3H]=O' to ensure the aldehyde group is directly connected to the aromatic ring.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]' is correct for nitro groups on aromatic rings, but ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly parsed to identify these groups.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern '[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' should be revised to ensure it captures the combination of sulfanyl and carboxylic acid groups effectively. Consider using a pattern like '[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' to ensure these groups are directly connected.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2][CH3]' is correct for methoxy groups on aromatic rings, but ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly parsed to identify these groups.

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][Br,NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid with aromatic and electron-withdrawing group
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][c,n]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic or heteroaromatic
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol group
        ['[C@H]1([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]1[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 8: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 9: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid group
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]']  # Rule 10: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][Br,NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid with aromatic and electron-withdrawing group
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][c,n]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic or heteroaromatic
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol group
        ['[C@H]1([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]1[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 8: Nitro group on aromatic ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 9: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid group
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]']  # Rule 10: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 8]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) with an aromatic ring, particularly when combined with an electron-withdrawing group such as bromine or nitro, tend to result in high yield. This combination can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups can enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield due to their strong coordination ability with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield. The basicity of the pyridine nitrogen might interfere with the catalyst's active site, reducing its effectiveness. Examples: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of the CF3 group might destabilize the catalyst or interfere with the reaction mechanism. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of these groups can enhance metal coordination and catalyst stability. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The electron-donating nature of the methoxy group might interfere with the catalyst's activity. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is a significant opportunity for improvement. The low validation accuracy indicates that the current rules are not capturing the complexity of the data, and refining these rules could potentially lead to better performance.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - The SHAP analysis highlights that Rule 6 and Rule 7 are consistently contributing to high loading predictions, even when the experimental values are low. This suggests that these rules might be too general or incorrectly weighted.
   - The SHAP values also indicate that the rules might not be accounting for certain molecular features that are important for accurate predictions.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - Re-evaluate Rule 6 and Rule 7, as they are contributing to overestimated loadings. Consider incorporating additional molecular features or conditions that could differentiate between high and low loading scenarios more effectively.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - For underestimated loadings, investigate if there are additional features or interactions that are not currently captured by the rules. This might involve looking into specific functional groups or molecular structures that are associated with high experimental loadings.

3. **Improve Generalization:**

These groups can enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The electron-donating nature of the methoxy group might interfere with the catalyst's activity. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) with an aromatic ring, particularly when combined with an electron-withdrawing group such as bromine, nitro, cyano, or trifluoromethyl, tend to result in high yield. This combination can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole, phenyl, naphthalene, or thiophene, tend to result in high yield. These groups can enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield due to their strong coordination ability with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other functional groups that can enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids or thiol groups. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of these groups can enhance metal coordination and catalyst stability. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][Br]', '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]', '[n]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 8
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']  # Rule 12
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 8, 9]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other functional groups that can enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids or thiol groups. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of these groups can enhance metal coordination and catalyst stability. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2 should focus on amino acids with additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups. The current pattern '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]', '[n]' does not specifically target amino acids. Consider using a pattern that captures the amino acid backbone with aromatic groups, such as '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c,n]'.
- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 4's pattern '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]' is too generic and may not capture sugar-like structures effectively. Consider using a pattern that captures multiple hydroxyl groups in a sugar-like arrangement, such as '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'.
- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 5 should account for pyridine rings specifically, but the current pattern '[n][c]' is too broad. Use a more specific pattern like '[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1' to capture pyridine rings.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 8's pattern '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]' correctly identifies nitro groups on aromatic rings. Ensure this pattern is applied correctly to match the rule.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 12's pattern '[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]' is too generic for identifying linear aliphatic chains. Use a pattern that captures long aliphatic chains without functional groups, such as '[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][Br,NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c,n]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1'],  # Rule 5
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 8
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']  # Rule 12
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 8, 9]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with an electron-withdrawing group such as bromine or nitro, tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield due to their strong coordination ability with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other functional groups that can enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids or thiol groups. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of these groups can enhance metal coordination and catalyst stability. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][Br]', '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]', '[c][n]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1'],  # Rule 5
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 8
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 11

                        row.append(-1)

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 5's SMARTS `['[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1']` should be revised to ensure it captures pyridine rings accurately. The current pattern may not account for pyridine rings combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination.

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current validation accuracy of 0.5143 is significantly lower than the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules are not effective enough in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The drop in validation accuracy indicates potential underfitting, where the model is not capturing the underlying patterns in the data. This could be due to overly simplistic rules or a lack of rules that capture important features.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - There are several instances where the predicted loading is high, but the experimental value is low. For example, molecules like C1=CC=C(C=C1)C[C@@H](C(=O)O)N and C(CC(=O)O)C(=O)CCC(=O)O have high predicted loadings but low experimental values. Rule6 and Rule7 have the most positive SHAP values for these cases, indicating they might be problematic.
   - Conversely, molecules like C([C@@H](C(=O)O)N)C(=O)O and C1=CC2=C(C=C1C(=O)O)C(=O)OC2=O have low predicted loadings but high experimental values. Rule6 and Rule7 also have the most negative SHAP values for these cases, suggesting they might need adjustment.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is a significant opportunity for improvement. The low validation accuracy indicates that the current rules are not capturing the necessary complexity of the data.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - The SHAP analysis highlights that Rule6 and Rule7 are consistently contributing to incorrect predictions. This suggests that these rules may need to be refined or re-evaluated to better align with the experimental data.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule6 (Trifluoromethyl group):** Consider revising this rule to account for additional structural features that might influence the loading. The current rule might be too broad, leading to overestimation.
   - **Rule7 (Aldehyde group):** This rule might need to be more specific about the context in which an aldehyde group leads to low yield. Consider interactions with other functional groups that might mitigate the negative impact.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule6 and Rule7:** These rules should be adjusted to better capture the conditions under which they lead to low predicted loadings. Consider incorporating additional features or interactions that could influence the outcome.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce new rules or modify existing ones to capture more complex interactions between functional groups and the catalyst. This could help address the underfitting issue and improve the model's ability to generalize.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently contribute to incorrect predictions and explore potential modifications or additions that could improve accuracy.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider adding new features to the feature matrix that capture more nuanced chemical properties or interactions. This could help improve the model's ability to predict loading more accurately.

By addressing these areas, the rules can be refined to better capture the complexity of the data, leading to improved accuracy and more reliable predictions.

    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with an electron-withdrawing group such as bromine or nitro, tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield due to their strong coordination ability with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other functional groups that can enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids or thiol groups. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of these groups can enhance metal coordination and catalyst stability. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield due to their strong coordination ability with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other functional groups that can enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids or thiol groups. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield. The combination of these groups can enhance metal coordination and catalyst stability. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[Br,c][c]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid on aromatic with bromine or nitro
        ['[NX3][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[C]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol group
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]', '[C]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[n][c]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][C]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Linear aliphatic chain > 6 carbons
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[SX2H][c]'],  # Rule 12: Thiol with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 13: Benzoic acid with hydroxyl
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 12, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with an electron-withdrawing group such as bromine or nitro, tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield due to their strong coordination ability with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other functional groups that can enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids or thiol groups. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some improvement in validation accuracy from 0.514 to 0.628, indicating that the rules are becoming more effective. However, the accuracy is still not optimal, suggesting that there is room for further refinement.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The previous validation accuracies were consistently around 0.76, but the current accuracy is lower. This could indicate that the model is underfitting, as it is not capturing the complexity of the data well enough. The consistent SHAP values across different molecules suggest that the rules might be too generalized and not capturing specific interactions effectively.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, such as `C1=CC(=CC=C1C(=O)O)S`, Rule 3 has a high positive SHAP value, indicating it might be overestimating the effect of thiol groups.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, such as `C(CC(=O)O)[C@@H](C(=O)O)N`, Rule 1 has a high negative SHAP value, suggesting it might be underestimating the effect of carboxylic acid groups on aromatic rings.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy from 0.514 to 0.628 suggests that the rules are improving, but the model is still not performing as well as previous iterations with a validation accuracy of 0.76. This indicates that while some rules are being refined, others may need further adjustment to improve generalization.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - The SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules, such as Rule 3 and Rule 1, may need refinement. Rule 3, which deals with thiol groups, often shows high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, suggesting it might be too aggressive in predicting high loading. Rule 1, which deals with carboxylic acid groups, shows high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, indicating it might be too conservative.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 3 (Thiol Groups):** Consider adding conditions or exceptions to Rule 3 to prevent overestimation of loading when thiol groups are present. This could involve considering the presence of other functional groups that might mitigate the effect of thiol groups.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 1 (Carboxylic Acid Groups):** Re-evaluate the conditions under which carboxylic acid groups on aromatic rings are considered low yield. Consider the influence of additional electron-withdrawing groups that might enhance the effect of carboxylic acids.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce more nuanced rules that consider the interaction between multiple functional groups rather than evaluating them in isolation. This could help address underfitting by capturing more complex patterns in the data.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use the insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine rules. For example, test the impact of modifying Rule 3 and Rule 1 on a subset of the data to see if it improves accuracy before applying changes to the entire dataset.

5. **Additional Considerations:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or rules that account for steric effects or the spatial arrangement of functional groups, as these can significantly impact catalyst loading and might not be fully captured by the current rules.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with an electron-withdrawing group such as bromine or nitro, tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield due to their strong coordination ability with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other functional groups that can enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids or thiol groups. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Advice 5**: Use SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine the rules. Start by modifying Rule 3 and Rule 1 on a subset of the dataset to observe changes in accuracy, and then apply successful modifications to the entire dataset.

- **Advice 6**: Consider adding rules that evaluate the spatial arrangement of functional groups. For example, if a functional group is positioned in a way that enhances its interaction with the catalyst, adjust the rule to reflect this increased potential for high yield.

These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]', '[Br]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2+0][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[NX3H2][CX3](=O)[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]', '[c][Br]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[C@H]1([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]([OX2H])[C@H]1[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[NX3H2][CX3](=O)[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some improvement in validation accuracy, reaching 0.6857 from previous lower values like 0.5143 and 0.6286. This suggests that the rules are becoming more effective in capturing the underlying patterns in the data.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The improvement in validation accuracy without a significant drop in test accuracy suggests that the model is not overfitting. However, the relatively low accuracy compared to the reference metrics indicates potential underfitting, where the model might not be capturing all the relevant features or interactions.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 7, Rule 9) might be contributing to overestimation. These rules should be scrutinized for potential adjustments.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 7, Rule 9) might be underestimating the loading. These rules need to be refined to better capture the conditions leading to high loading.

4. **Accuracy Improvements Interpretation:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy suggests that the current rules are moving in the right direction. However, the gap between validation and test accuracy indicates room for further improvement, particularly in generalizing the rules to unseen data.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that consistently contribute to incorrect predictions. For instance, Rule 6 and Rule 7 often have high SHAP values for high loading predictions, indicating they might be too aggressive in predicting high loading.
   - Rule 9, associated with low yield predictions, might need adjustments to better differentiate between low and high yield scenarios.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Re-evaluate Rule 6 and Rule 7, which frequently contribute to overestimated loadings. Consider incorporating additional conditions or modifying the existing ones to reduce their influence on high loading predictions.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - For rules like Rule 9, which contribute to underestimated loadings, explore additional features or interactions that might indicate high loading. This could involve integrating more complex interactions or considering additional chemical properties.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential underfitting, consider expanding the feature set or exploring more complex rule interactions. This could involve using domain knowledge to identify additional relevant features or interactions that are currently not captured by the rules.

4. **Iterative Refinement Using SHAP Insights:**
   - Use SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules with consistently high SHAP values for incorrect predictions and explore ways to adjust their conditions or thresholds.
   - Consider cross-validation techniques to ensure that rule adjustments lead to consistent improvements across different data subsets.

5. **Incorporate Domain Expertise:**
   - Engage with domain experts to validate the chemical relevance of the rules and explore potential new rules that might capture overlooked interactions or features.

By implementing these recommendations, the rules can be refined to improve both the accuracy and generalization of the model, leading to more reliable predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

    Target Name: yield

    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]', '[Br]', '[Cl]', '[F]', '[I]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]', '[n]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][C]', '[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern should include the presence of a carboxylic acid group attached to an aromatic ring and strong electron-withdrawing groups like nitro or halogens. The current SMARTS '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' does not account for the presence of electron-withdrawing groups. Consider adding patterns for nitro '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]' and halogens '[Br]', '[Cl]', '[F]', '[I]' to ensure the rule is correctly applied.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2 mentions amino acid structures with additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups. The SMARTS '[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][C]' does not capture the aromatic or heteroaromatic groups. Consider adding patterns for aromatic rings '[c]' and heteroaromatic rings '[n]' to better match the rule description.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4 involves multiple hydroxyl groups in a sugar-like structure. The current SMARTS '[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][C]' is repeated and may not accurately capture the sugar-like structure. Consider using a pattern that captures multiple hydroxyl groups in a cyclic or linear sugar-like arrangement.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5 requires a pyridine ring with a carboxylic acid group. The SMARTS '[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' should be checked to ensure it captures the pyridine structure correctly.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6 involves a trifluoromethyl group. The SMARTS '[CX4](F)(F)F' is correct, but ensure it is part of a larger electron-withdrawing system if exceptions are needed.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7 involves an aldehyde group on an aromatic ring. The SMARTS '[c][CX3H]=O' should be checked to ensure it captures the aromatic aldehyde structure correctly.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12 involves a sulfanyl group and an aromatic ring. The SMARTS '[c][SX2H]' should be checked to ensure it captures the structure correctly.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13 involves a benzoic acid structure with an additional hydroxyl group. The SMARTS '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]' should be checked to ensure it captures the structure correctly.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15 involves a nitro group on an aromatic ring. The SMARTS '[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]' should be checked to ensure it captures the structure correctly.
