Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]', '[Br]', '[Cl]', '[F]', '[I]'],  # Rule 1
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]', '[n]'],  # Rule 2
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][C]', '[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 4
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 10
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 13
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 15
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some improvement in validation accuracy, reaching 0.6857, which is higher than some previous iterations (e.g., 0.5143 and 0.6286). This suggests that the rules are becoming more effective in capturing the underlying patterns in the data.
   - However, the test accuracy has not been provided for the current iteration, making it difficult to fully assess the generalization capability of the model.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The improvement in validation accuracy suggests that the model is learning from the data, but without test accuracy, it's challenging to determine if overfitting is occurring.
   - The consistent improvement in validation accuracy across iterations indicates that the model might be underfitting less as rules are refined.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 7, Rule 9) might be contributing to overestimation.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 7, Rule 9) might be contributing to underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy suggests that the probability of improvement for the current rules is high. However, further iterations and test set evaluations are necessary to confirm this trend.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 7, Rule 9) have a significant impact on the predictions. These rules should be closely examined and refined to improve prediction accuracy.
   - The consistent SHAP values across different molecules suggest that these rules are either too general or not capturing specific interactions effectively.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loadings:**
   - Rules with high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, such as Rule 6 (trifluoromethyl group) and Rule 7 (aldehyde group), should be refined. Consider adding conditions or exceptions to these rules to better capture the nuances of the data.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loadings:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 9 (linear aliphatic chain), should be adjusted. Explore additional features or interactions that might be missing from these rules.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential overfitting, consider simplifying some rules or combining similar rules to reduce complexity. This can help improve the model's ability to generalize to unseen data.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values across different molecules and adjust them based on experimental feedback.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or modifying existing ones to capture more complex interactions. This could involve exploring new chemical properties or structural features that are not currently included in the rules.

By following these recommendations, the current rules can be refined to improve both the accuracy and generalization of the model, ultimately leading to better predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

Final Metric Message:

    Target Name: yield
    GPT Model: gpt-4o-2024-08-06
    ML Model: ETC
    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield. The aldehyde group can potentially react with other components in the reaction mixture, reducing the availability of the catalyst. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. When combined with additional electron-withdrawing groups like carbonyls or nitro groups, they may contribute to high yield. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. However, the presence of polar or coordinating groups like hydroxyl or amino groups can enhance yield. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]', '[Br]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic carboxylic acid with nitro or halogens
        ['[NX3H2+0][C][C](=O)[O]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sugar-like structure
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F', '[CX3](=O)', '[NX3+](=O)'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl with electron-withdrawing groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][OX2]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Thiol with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Benzoic acid with hydroxyl
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine with thiol
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 12 **: For Rule 12, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][SX2H]']` is correct for thiol with an aromatic ring, but ensure that the thiol group is not part of a larger structure that might interfere with the rule.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]']` should be revised to ensure that the benzoic acid structure has an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern like `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]']`.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: For Rule 14, the SMARTS pattern `['[n][SX2H]']` is correct for pyridine with thiol, but ensure that the thiol group is not part of a larger structure that might interfere with the rule.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: For Rule 15, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']` is correct for nitro on an aromatic ring, but ensure that the nitro group is not part of a larger structure that might interfere with the rule.

** End of Suggestions **
---------------------------------------------------------------
Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]', '[Br,Cl,I,F]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic carboxylic acid with nitro or halogens
        ['[NX3H2+0][C][C](=O)[O]', '[c]', '[c][n]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic or heteroaromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]', '[C@H]'],  # Rule 4: Sugar-like structure
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F', '[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl with electron-withdrawing groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]', '[!#6]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]', '[C][C][C]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][OX2]', '[C][C]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Thiol with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Benzoic acid with hydroxyl
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine with thiol
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. When combined with additional electron-withdrawing groups like carbonyls or nitro groups, they may contribute to high yield. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. However, the presence of polar or coordinating groups like hydroxyl or amino groups can enhance yield. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) or halogens (e.g., bromine), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. When combined with additional electron-withdrawing groups like carbonyls or nitro groups, they may contribute to high yield. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. However, the presence of polar or coordinating groups like hydroxyl or amino groups can enhance yield. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. When combined with additional electron-withdrawing groups like carbonyls or nitro groups, they may contribute to high yield. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. However, the presence of polar or coordinating groups like hydroxyl or amino groups can enhance yield. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid on aromatic ring with nitro group
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][c]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol group with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][C]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Linear aliphatic chain > 6 carbons
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido group with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Thiol group with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Benzoic acid with additional hydroxyl group
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine ring with thiol group
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]', '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid on aromatic ring with nitro group
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][c]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol group with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F', '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group with electron-withdrawing system
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Linear aliphatic chain > 6 carbons
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido group with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Thiol group with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Benzoic acid with additional hydroxyl group
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine ring with thiol group
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. When combined with additional electron-withdrawing groups like carbonyls or nitro groups, they may contribute to high yield. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. However, the presence of polar or coordinating groups like hydroxyl or amino groups can enhance yield. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]', '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid on aromatic ring with nitro group
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+][C][C][c]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol group with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F', '[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group with electron-withdrawing system
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Linear aliphatic chain > 6 carbons
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido group with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][SX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Thiol group with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Benzoic acid with additional hydroxyl group
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine ring with thiol group
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 12, 14]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to have mixed effectiveness. The validation accuracy has fluctuated significantly across iterations, with the latest accuracy at 0.5429, which is lower than some previous iterations. This suggests that the rules may not be consistently capturing the underlying patterns in the data.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The fluctuation in validation accuracy indicates potential issues with overfitting or underfitting. The model's performance does not consistently improve, suggesting that the rules may not be generalizing well across different datasets.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 7 often has a high positive SHAP value, indicating it might be contributing to overestimation.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 7 also shows significant negative SHAP values, suggesting it might be contributing to underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement. The current rules do not consistently lead to high validation accuracy, indicating that the rules may need refinement to better capture the relationship between features and outcomes.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that Rule 7, which involves modifiers with an aldehyde group on an aromatic ring, is frequently associated with discrepancies in predictions. This rule might need refinement to better account for the context in which aldehyde groups contribute to high or low loading.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - Rule 7 should be revisited and potentially split into more specific sub-rules that account for the presence of additional functional groups that might mitigate or exacerbate the effect of the aldehyde group.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - Rules that consistently show high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 7, should be adjusted to better capture the conditions under which these modifiers lead to high loading.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or modifying existing rules to improve the model's ability to generalize across different datasets. This might involve integrating more complex interactions between functional groups or considering the spatial arrangement of atoms.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. This could involve testing new hypotheses about the interactions between functional groups and their impact on catalyst loading, and then validating these hypotheses with additional data.

5. **Incorporate Domain Knowledge:**
   - Collaborate with domain experts to incorporate more nuanced chemical insights into the rules. This could help in identifying overlooked factors that influence catalyst loading and improve the model's predictive power.

By addressing these areas, the rules can be refined to better capture the complex relationships in the data, leading to improved model performance and more reliable predictions.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Examples: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Examples: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. When combined with additional electron-withdrawing groups like carbonyls or nitro groups, they may contribute to high yield. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. However, the presence of polar or coordinating groups like hydroxyl or amino groups can enhance yield. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Examples: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid, 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. However, the presence of polar or coordinating groups like hydroxyl or amino groups can enhance yield. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid on aromatic ring with nitro group
        ['[NX3H2+0][C][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyls
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Linear aliphatic chain > 6 carbons
        ['[NX3H2][CX3](=O)[CX3H2]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][OX2]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Benzoic acid with hydroxyl
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Pyridine with thiol
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 14: Nitro on aromatic ring
        ['[c][SX2H]']  # Rule 15: Sulfanyl on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 13, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid on aromatic ring with nitro group
        ['[NX3H2+0][C][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyls
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Linear aliphatic chain > 6 carbons
        ['[NX3H2][CX3](=O)[CX3H2]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][OX2]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Benzoic acid with hydroxyl
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Pyridine with thiol
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 14: Nitro on aromatic ring
        ['[c][SX2H]']  # Rule 15: Sulfanyl on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 13, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Example: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid on aromatic ring with nitro group
        ['[NX3H2+0][C][C][C][C][C][C]', '[c]'],  # Rule 2: Amino acid with aromatic group
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Thiol with carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyls
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 7: Aldehyde on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2][CH3]'],  # Rule 8: Methoxy on aromatic ring
        ['[C][C][C][C][C][C][C]'],  # Rule 9: Linear aliphatic chain > 6 carbons
        ['[NX3H2][CX3](=O)[CX3H2]'],  # Rule 10: Acetamido with amino group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2][C][C][OX2]'],  # Rule 11: Carboxylic acid with ether linkage
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Benzoic acid with hydroxyl
        ['[n][SX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Pyridine with thiol
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)-[OX-]'],  # Rule 14: Nitro on aromatic ring
        ['[c][SX2H]']  # Rule 15: Sulfanyl on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 13, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Example: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some effectiveness, as indicated by the validation accuracy of 0.5714. However, this is still below the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules may not be capturing all the necessary features or interactions to accurately predict the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting:**
   - The fluctuating validation accuracies across iterations (ranging from 0.5143 to 0.6857) suggest potential issues with overfitting or underfitting. The model may be overfitting to specific features captured by the rules, as indicated by the high SHAP values for certain rules, leading to discrepancies between predicted and experimental values.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 7 and Rule 9) may be problematic. These rules might be overemphasizing certain features that do not contribute to high loading in practice.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 4 and Rule 6) may need adjustment, as they might be underestimating the contribution of certain features.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement. The model's performance has not consistently improved across iterations, indicating that the rules may not be fully optimized or that additional features need to be considered.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules (e.g., Rule 7 and Rule 9) consistently have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, suggesting these rules may need refinement to reduce their influence on the model.
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings (e.g., Rule 4 and Rule 6) should be adjusted to better capture the features that contribute to high loading.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Rules:**
   - Re-evaluate and refine rules with high positive SHAP values, such as Rule 7 (aldehyde group on aromatic ring) and Rule 9 (linear aliphatic chain), to ensure they are not overemphasizing features that do not contribute to high loading.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Rules:**
   - Modify rules with high negative SHAP values, such as Rule 4 (multiple hydroxyl groups) and Rule 6 (trifluoromethyl group), to better capture their potential positive contributions to loading.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or interactions that may not be currently captured by the rules. This could involve exploring new chemical groups or structural motifs that influence loading.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. This could involve testing new hypotheses about feature interactions and adjusting rules based on their impact on model performance.

5. **Evaluate Rule Effectiveness:**
   - Continuously evaluate the effectiveness of refined rules by monitoring changes in validation accuracy and SHAP values. This will help ensure that the rules are contributing positively to the model's predictive power.

By addressing these areas, the current rules can be improved to better capture the complex interactions that determine the loading of modifiers on catalysts, ultimately leading to more accurate predictions.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) attached to an aromatic ring, especially when combined with strong electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2), tend to result in high yield. These groups can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with an amino acid structure that includes additional aromatic or heteroaromatic groups, such as indole or phenyl, tend to result in high yield. These groups enhance coordination with the metal center, improving catalyst activity. Example: (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a thiol group (SH) tend to result in high yield, especially when combined with other functional groups that enhance metal coordination, such as carboxylic acids. Example: 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure, tend to result in high yield. These groups can form strong hydrogen bonds, potentially stabilizing the catalyst structure. Example: (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination. Example: pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (CF3) tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a larger electron-withdrawing system that can stabilize the catalyst. Example: 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with an aldehyde group (CHO) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are part of a structure that includes additional electron-donating groups that can mitigate the negative impact of the aldehyde. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a methoxy group (OCH3) on an aromatic ring tend to result in low yield unless they are combined with other strong electron-withdrawing groups that can offset the electron-donating nature of the methoxy group. Example: 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a linear aliphatic chain of more than six carbon atoms without additional functional groups tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an acetamido group (NHCOCH3) combined with an amino group (NH2) on a linear aliphatic chain tend to result in low yield. This combination may not provide sufficient interaction with the catalyst. Example: (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an ether linkage (O) in a linear chain tend to result in low yield, possibly due to insufficient coordination with the catalyst. Example: 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a benzoic acid structure and an additional hydroxyl group on the aromatic ring tend to result in low yield, potentially due to competitive binding or deactivation of the catalyst. Example: 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a thiol group tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) on an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the nitro group can stabilize the Fe ion in the catalyst, enhancing its reactivity. Example: 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (SH) and an aromatic ring tend to result in high yield due to enhanced metal coordination and stabilization of the catalyst. Example: 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid.
